</p><p>As a result of Persian trade in China, and the battle of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Talas" title="Battle of Talas">Talas River</a>, Chinese innovations entered the Islamic intellectual world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup> These include advances in astronomy and in <a href="/wiki/History_of_paper" title="History of paper">paper-making</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-meggs58_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-meggs58-103">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasood2009132–135_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasood2009132–135-104">[102]</a></sup> Paper-making spread through the Islamic World as far west as <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Islamic Spain</a>, before paper-making was acquired for Europe by the <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup> There is debate about <a href="/wiki/History_of_gunpowder#Spread_throughout_Eurasia_and_Africa" title="History of gunpowder">transmission of gunpowder</a> on whether the Mongols introduced <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_of_the_Song_dynasty#Gunpowder_warfare" title="Science and technology of the Song dynasty">Chinese gunpowder weapons</a> to Europe or if gunpowder weapons were invented in Europe independently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup>Within Eurasia transfer of information between world cultures did occur, usally through translations of written documents. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literate_culture_and_arts">Literate culture and arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Literate culture and arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_literature" title="History of literature">History of literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_art" title="History of art">History of art</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_music" title="History of music">History of music</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Genji_emaki_azumaya.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2501" data-file-width="4578" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Genji_emaki_azumaya.jpg/220px-Genji_emaki_azumaya.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Genji_emaki_azumaya.jpg/330px-Genji_emaki_azumaya.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Genji_emaki_azumaya.jpg/440px-Genji_emaki_azumaya.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Genji_emaki_azumaya.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>12th century illustration from the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tale_of_Genji" title="The Tale of Genji">Tale of Genji</a></i>, the world's first novel.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><audio class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="11" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Talaei-tetrachords.ogg" id="mwe_player_2" preload="none" style="width:220px;" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="98126" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (98 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e2/Talaei-tetrachords.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="152816" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/e/e2/Talaei-tetrachords.ogg/Talaei-tetrachords.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/></audio> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Talaei-tetrachords.ogg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Persian Talaei-tetrachords</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><audio class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="71" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Ut_Queant_Laxis.ogg" id="mwe_player_3" preload="none" style="width:220px;" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="78369" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (78 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/93/Ut_Queant_Laxis.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="126136" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/9/93/Ut_Queant_Laxis.ogg/Ut_Queant_Laxis.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/></audio> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ut_Queant_Laxis.ogg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Italy, 8th century <i>Ut Queant Laxis</i></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><audio class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="87" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Spc206_beholdwaterofwaters_dwd_128kb_1.ogg" id="mwe_player_4" preload="none" style="width:220px;" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="67045" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (67 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d1/Spc206_beholdwaterofwaters_dwd_128kb_1.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/></audio> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spc206_beholdwaterofwaters_dwd_128kb_1.ogg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Behold Water of Waters, by Iranian poet <a href="/wiki/Rumi" title="Rumi">Rumi</a>. Example of lyric poetry</div></div></div>
<p>Within Eurasia, there were four major civilization groups that had literate cultures and created literature and arts, including Europe, the Middle East, South Asia and East Asia. Southeast Asia could be a possible fifth category but was influenced heavily from both South and East Asia literal cultures. All four cultures in Post-Classical Times used <a href="/wiki/Poetry" title="Poetry">poetry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drama" title="Drama">drama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prose" title="Prose">prose</a>. Throughout the period and until the 19th century poetry was the dominant form of literary expression. In the Middle East, South Asia, Europe and China great poetic works often used figurative language. Examples include, the <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Shakuntala_(play)" title="Shakuntala (play)">Shakuntala</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> <i><a href="/wiki/One_Thousand_and_One_Nights" title="One Thousand and One Nights">Thousand and one nights</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Beowulf" title="Beowulf">Beowulf</a> </i> and works by the Chinese <a href="/wiki/Du_Fu" title="Du Fu">Du Fu</a>. In Japan, prose uniquely thrived more than in other geographic areas. The <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tale_of_Genji" title="The Tale of Genji">Tale of Genji</a></i> is considered the world's first realistic novel written in the 9th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup>
</p><p>Musically, most regions of the world only used <a href="/wiki/Melody" title="Melody">melodies</a> as opposed to <a href="/wiki/Harmony" title="Harmony">harmony</a>. Medieval Europe was the lone exception to this rule, developing harmonic music in the 14th/15th century as musical culture transitioned form sacred music (meant for the church) to secular music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup> South Asian and Mid-Eastern music were similar to each other for their use of <a href="/wiki/Microtonal_music" title="Microtonal music">microtone</a>. East-Asian music shared some similarities with European Music for using a <a href="/wiki/Pentatonic_scale" title="Pentatonic scale">pentatonic scale</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History_by_region_in_the_Old_World">History by region in the Old World</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: History by region in the Old World">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Africa#500_to_1800" title="History of Africa">Medieval Africa</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Djenne_Terracotta_Equestrian_(13th-15th_cent).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="450" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Djenne_Terracotta_Equestrian_%2813th-15th_cent%29.jpg/220px-Djenne_Terracotta_Equestrian_%2813th-15th_cent%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Djenne_Terracotta_Equestrian_%2813th-15th_cent%29.jpg/330px-Djenne_Terracotta_Equestrian_%2813th-15th_cent%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Djenne_Terracotta_Equestrian_%2813th-15th_cent%29.jpg/440px-Djenne_Terracotta_Equestrian_%2813th-15th_cent%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Djenne_Terracotta_Equestrian_(13th-15th_cent).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Djenne Terracotta Equestrian (13th–15th century), within the <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a></div></div></div>
<p>During the Postclassical Era, <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> was both culturally and politically affected by the introduction of Islam and the Arabic empires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearnsAdasSchwartzGilbert2011184_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearnsAdasSchwartzGilbert2011184-111">[109]</a></sup> This was especially true in the north, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sudan_region" title="Sudan region">Sudan region</a>, and the east coast. However, this conversion was not complete nor uniform among different areas, and the low-level classes hardly changed their beliefs at all.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metmuseum_islam_trade_and_spread_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-metmuseum_islam_trade_and_spread-112">[110]</a></sup> Prior to the migration and conquest of Muslims into Africa, much of the continent was dominated by diverse societies of varying sizes and complexities. These were ruled by kings or councils of elders who would control their constituents in a variety of ways. Most of these peoples practiced spiritual, animistic religions. Africa was culturally separated between Saharan Africa (which consisted of <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara Desert</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a> (everything south of the Sahara). Sub-Saharan Africa was further divided into the <a href="/wiki/Sudan_(region)" title="Sudan (region)">Sudan</a>, which covered everything north of <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a>, including <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>. The area south of the Sudan was primarily occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a> who spoke the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bantu_language" title="Bantu language">Bantu language</a>. From 1100 onward <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">Christian Europe</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_World" title="Islamic World">Islamic World</a> became dependent on Africa for gold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003136_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003136-113">[111]</a></sup>
</p><p>After approximately 650 urbanization expanded for the first time beyond the ancient kingdoms <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aksum" title="Kingdom of Aksum">Aksum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nubia" title="Nubia">Nubia</a>. African civilizations can be divided into three categories based on religion:
</p>
<ul><li>Christian civilizations on the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a>,</li>
<li>Islamic civilizations which formed in the Niger River valley in West Africa, and on the coast of East Africa, and</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Traditional_society" title="Traditional society">traditional societies</a> which adhered to native African religions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup> South of the Sahara African kingdoms developed based on continental trade with one another through land based routes and generally avoided sea trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003136_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003136-113">[111]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Sub-Saharan Africa was part of two large, separate trading networks, the Trans Saharan trade which bridged commerce between West and North Africa. Due to the huge profits from trade native African Islamic empires arose, including those of <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Empire" title="Ghana Empire">Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Songhai_Empire" title="Songhai Empire">Songhay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup> In the 14th century, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Musa_I_of_Mali" title="Musa I of Mali">Mansa Musa</a> king of Mali may have been the wealthiest person of his time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> Within Mali, the city of <a href="/wiki/Timbuktu" title="Timbuktu">Timbuktu</a> was an international center of science and well known throughout the Islamic World, particularly from the <a href="/wiki/Sankore_Madrasah" title="Sankore Madrasah">University of Sankore</a>.
East Africa was part of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean_trade" title="Indian Ocean trade">Indian Ocean trade network</a>, which included both Arab ruled Islamic cities on the East African Coast such as <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a> and Traditional cities such as <a href="/wiki/Great_Zimbabwe" title="Great Zimbabwe">Great Zimbabwe</a> which exported gold, copper and ivory to markets in the Middle East, South Asia, and Southeast Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003136_113-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003136-113">[111]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a></div><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Medieval_ploughing.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="434" data-file-width="472" decoding="async" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Medieval_ploughing.JPG/200px-Medieval_ploughing.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Medieval_ploughing.JPG/300px-Medieval_ploughing.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Medieval_ploughing.JPG/400px-Medieval_ploughing.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Medieval_ploughing.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Medieval ploughing. Most Europeans in the Middle Ages were landless peasants called <i><a href="/wiki/Serfdom" title="Serfdom">serfs</a></i> who worked in exchange for military protection. After the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a> of the 1340s, a labor shortage caused serfs to demand wages for their labor. Drawing from 1300</div></div></div><p>In Europe, Western civilization reconstituted after the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Western_Roman_Empire" title="Fall of the Western Roman Empire">Fall of the Western Roman Empire</a> into the period now known as the <a href="/wiki/Early_Middle_Ages" title="Early Middle Ages">Early Middle Ages</a> (500–1000). The Early Middle Ages saw a continuation of trends begun in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_Antiquity" title="Late Antiquity">Late Antiquity</a>: depopulation, deurbanization, and increased <a href="/wiki/Barbarian" title="Barbarian">barbarian</a> invasion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clark_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-clark-117">[115]</a></sup>
</p><p>From the 7th until the 11th centuries <a href="/wiki/Early_Muslim_conquests" title="Early Muslim conquests">Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarians" title="Hungarians">Magyars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Viking_Age" title="Viking Age">Norse</a> were all threats to the Christian Kingdoms that killed thousands of people over centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016291_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016291-118">[116]</a></sup> Raiders however, also created new trading networks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016429_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016429-119">[117]</a></sup> In western Europe the Frankish king <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> attempted to kindle the rise of culture and science in the <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Renaissance" title="Carolingian Renaissance">Carolingian Renaissance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016284_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016284-120">[118]</a></sup> In the year 800 <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> founded the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> in attempt to resurrect <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_Rome" title="Classical Rome">Classical Rome</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016282–283_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016282–283-121">[119]</a></sup> The reign of Charlemagne attempted to kindle a rise of learning and literacy in what has become known as the <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Renaissance" title="Carolingian Renaissance">Carolingian Renaissance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016282_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016282-122">[120]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Eastern Europe, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Empire" title="Eastern Roman Empire">Eastern Roman Empire</a> survived in what is now called the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> which created the <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Juris_Civilis" title="Corpus Juris Civilis">Code of Justinian</a> that inspired the legal structures of modern European states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016272_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016272-123">[121]</a></sup> Overseen by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christianity" title="Orthodox Christianity">Christian Orthodox</a> emperors, in the 9th-10th centuries the Byzantine <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a> christianized the <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">First Bulgarian Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus'">Kievan Rus</a>, the cultural and political ancestors to modern-day <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a>, on the one hand, and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, on the other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Byzantium" title="Byzantium">Byzantium</a> flourished as the leading power and trade center in its region in the <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Renaissance" title="Macedonian Renaissance">Macedonian Renaissance</a> until it was overshadowed by <a href="/wiki/Italian_city-states" title="Italian city-states">Italian City States</a> and the Islamic <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> near the end of the Middle Ages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016285_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016285-127">[125]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bobolice,_zamek.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2200" data-file-width="3400" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Bobolice%2C_zamek.jpg/220px-Bobolice%2C_zamek.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Bobolice%2C_zamek.jpg/330px-Bobolice%2C_zamek.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Bobolice%2C_zamek.jpg/440px-Bobolice%2C_zamek.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bobolice,_zamek.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bobolice_Castle" title="Bobolice Castle">Bobolice Castle</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Bobolice" title="Bobolice">Boblice Poland</a>. <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Medieval European</a> castles were centers of <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudal power.</a></div></div></div>
<p>Later in the period, the creation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feudal_system" title="Feudal system">feudal system</a> allowed greater degrees of military and agricultural organization. There was sustained <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanization</a> in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Europe" title="Northern Europe">northern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">western Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016433_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016433-128">[126]</a></sup> Later developments were marked by <a href="/wiki/Manorialism" title="Manorialism">manorialism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudalism</a>, and evolved into the prosperous <a href="/wiki/High_Middle_Ages" title="High Middle Ages">High Middle Ages</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016433_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016433-128">[126]</a></sup> After 1000 the Christian kingdoms that had emerged from Rome's collapse changed dramatically in their cultural and societal character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016429_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016429-119">[117]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the High Middle Ages (c. 1000–1300), <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a>-oriented art and architecture flourished and the <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">Crusades</a> were mounted to recapture the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">Holy Land</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016444_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016444-129">[127]</a></sup> The influence of the emerging <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nation-state" title="Nation-state">nation-state</a> was tempered by the ideal of an international <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">Christendom</a> and the presence of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> in all western kingdoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003122–123_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003122–123-130">[128]</a></sup> The codes of <a href="/wiki/Chivalry" title="Chivalry">chivalry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Courtly_love" title="Courtly love">courtly love</a> set rules for proper behavior, while the <a href="/wiki/Scholasticism" title="Scholasticism">Scholastic</a> philosophers attempted to reconcile faith and reason.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016451_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016451-101">[99]</a></sup> The age of Feudalism would be dramatically transformed by the cataclysm of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a> and its aftermath.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003142_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003142-131">[129]</a></sup> This time would be a major underlying cause for the Renaissance. By the turn of the 16th century European or <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western Civilization</a> would be engaging in the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016477_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016477-132">[130]</a></sup>
</p><p>The term "Middle Ages" first appears in Latin in the 15th century and reflects the view that this period was a deviation from the path of <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical learning</a>, a path supposedly reconnected by <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> scholarship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miglio112_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Miglio112-133">[131]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="West_Asia">West Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: West Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medieval_Middle_East" title="Medieval Middle East">Medieval Middle East</a></div>
<p>The Arabian peninsula and the surrounding <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">Near East</a> regions saw dramatic change during the Postclassical Era caused primarily by the spread of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">Arabian Empires</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BD-%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%94%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B5.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BD-%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%94%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B5.jpg/220px-%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BD-%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%94%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BD-%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%94%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B5.jpg/330px-%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BD-%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%94%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BD-%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%94%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B5.jpg/440px-%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BD-%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%94%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B5.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BD-%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%94%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>6th century Sassanid defense lines in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Derbent" title="Derbent">Derbent, Dagestan Russia</a></div></div></div>
<p>In the 5th century, the Middle East was separated by empires and their spheres of influence; the two most prominent were the Persian <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sasanian Empire</a>, centered in what is now <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> in <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>). The Byzantines and Sasanians fought with each other continually, a reflection of the rivalry between the Roman Empire and the Persian Empire seen during the previous five hundred years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> The fighting weakened both states, leaving the stage open to a new power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the nomadic <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">Bedouin</a> tribes who dominated the Arabian desert saw a period of tribal warfare for scarce resources and a familiarity with Abrahamic religions or monotheism. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3681" data-file-width="5514" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg/220px-Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg/330px-Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg/440px-Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Hagia_Sophia" title="Hagia Sophia">Hagia Sophia</a> in Constantinople was the center of the Orthodox Church in the Byzantine Empire</div></div></div>
<p>While the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> Roman and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanian_Empire" title="Sassanian Empire">Sassanid</a> Persian empires were both weakened by the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine%E2%80%93Sasanian_War_of_602%E2%80%93628" title="Byzantine–Sasanian War of 602–628">Byzantine–Sasanian War of 602–628</a>, a new power in the form of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> grew in the Middle East under <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_in_Medina" title="Muhammad in Medina">Muhammad in Medina</a>. In a series of rapid <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim_conquests" title="Muslim conquests">Muslim conquests</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rashidun_army" title="Rashidun army">Rashidun army</a>, led by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caliph" title="Caliph">Caliphs</a> and skilled military commanders such as <a href="/wiki/Khalid_ibn_al-Walid" title="Khalid ibn al-Walid">Khalid ibn al-Walid</a>, swept through most of the Middle East, taking more than half of Byzantine territory in the <a href="/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Byzantine_wars" title="Arab–Byzantine wars">Arab–Byzantine wars</a> and completely engulfing Persia in the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Persia" title="Muslim conquest of Persia">Muslim conquest of Persia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the nomadic <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">Bedouin</a> tribes who dominated the Arabian desert saw a period of tribal warfare for scarce resources and a familiarity with Abrahamic religions or monotheism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup>  It would be the Arab <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">Caliphates</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> that would first unify the entire Middle East as a distinct region and create the dominant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">ethnic identity</a> that persists today. These Caliphates included the <a href="/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate" title="Rashidun Caliphate">Rashidun Caliphate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad Caliphate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasid Caliphate</a>, and later the Turkic-based <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seljuq_Empire" title="Seljuq Empire">Seljuq Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:15th_century_egyptian_anatomy_of_horse.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1371" data-file-width="992" decoding="async" height="276" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/15th_century_egyptian_anatomy_of_horse.jpg/200px-15th_century_egyptian_anatomy_of_horse.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/15th_century_egyptian_anatomy_of_horse.jpg/299px-15th_century_egyptian_anatomy_of_horse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/15th_century_egyptian_anatomy_of_horse.jpg/399px-15th_century_egyptian_anatomy_of_horse.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:15th_century_egyptian_anatomy_of_horse.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Anatomy of a horse from the 15th century. The <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">Golden Age of Islam</a> made advances in <a href="/wiki/Medicine_in_the_medieval_Islamic_world" title="Medicine in the medieval Islamic world">medicine</a>. From the University Library, Istanbul.</div></div></div>
<p>After Muhammad introduced Islam, it jump-started Middle Eastern culture into an <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">Islamic Golden Age</a>, inspiring achievements in <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a>, the revival of old advances in science and technology, and the formation of a distinct way of life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup> Muslims saved and spread Greek advances in <a href="/wiki/History_of_medicine" title="History of medicine">medicine</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_elementary_algebra" title="History of elementary algebra">algebra</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_geometry" title="History of geometry">geometry</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_astronomy" title="History of astronomy">astronomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_anatomy" title="History of anatomy">anatomy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_ethics" title="History of ethics">ethics</a> that would later finds it way back to Western Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup>
</p><p>The dominance of the Arabs came to a sudden end in the mid-11th century with the arrival of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seljuq_Turks" title="Seljuq Turks">Seljuq Turks</a>, migrating south from the Turkic homelands in Central Asia. They conquered Persia, Iraq (capturing Baghdad in 1055), Syria, Palestine, and the <a href="/wiki/Hejaz" title="Hejaz">Hejaz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> This was followed by a series of Christian Western Europe invasions. The fragmentation of the Middle East allowed joint European forces mainly from <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">France</a>, and the emerging <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, to enter the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016328_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016328-144">[142]</a></sup> In 1099 the knights of the <a href="/wiki/First_Crusade" title="First Crusade">First Crusade</a> captured <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> and founded the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Jerusalem" title="Kingdom of Jerusalem">Kingdom of Jerusalem</a>, which survived until 1187, when <a href="/wiki/Saladin" title="Saladin">Saladin</a> retook the city. Smaller crusader fiefdoms survived until 1291.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016331_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016331-145">[143]</a></sup> In the early 13th century, a new wave of invaders, the armies of the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a>, swept through the region, sacking Baghdad in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Baghdad_(1258)" title="Siege of Baghdad (1258)">Siege of Baghdad (1258)</a> and advancing as far south as the border of <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> in what became known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_conquests" title="Mongol conquests">Mongol conquests</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016333_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016333-146">[144]</a></sup> The Mongols eventually retreated in 1335, but the chaos that ensued throughout the empire deposed the Seljuq Turks. In 1401, the region was further plagued by the <a href="/wiki/Turco-Mongol_tradition" title="Turco-Mongol tradition">Turko-Mongol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timur" title="Timur">Timur</a>, and his ferocious raids. By then, another group of Turks had arisen as well, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turks" title="Ottoman Turks">Ottomans</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Asia">South Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: South Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Medieval_India" title="Medieval India">Medieval India</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_India#Classical_to_early_medieval_periods_(c._200_BCE_–_c._1200_CE)" title="History of India">History of India § Classical to early medieval periods (c. 200 BCE – c. 1200 CE)</a>, and <a href="#Late_medieval_period_(c._1200–1526_CE)">§ Late medieval period (c. 1200–1526 CE)</a></div>
<p>There has been difficulty applying the word 'medieval' or 'post classical' to the history of South Asia. This section follows historian Stein Burton's definition that corresponds from the 8th century to the 16th century, more of less following the same time frame of the Post Classical Period and the European Middle Ages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thanjuvur_Peruvudayar_Temple_(_Big_Temple).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3759" data-file-width="2584" decoding="async" height="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Thanjuvur_Peruvudayar_Temple_%28_Big_Temple%29.jpg/220px-Thanjuvur_Peruvudayar_Temple_%28_Big_Temple%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Thanjuvur_Peruvudayar_Temple_%28_Big_Temple%29.jpg/330px-Thanjuvur_Peruvudayar_Temple_%28_Big_Temple%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Thanjuvur_Peruvudayar_Temple_%28_Big_Temple%29.jpg/440px-Thanjuvur_Peruvudayar_Temple_%28_Big_Temple%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thanjuvur_Peruvudayar_Temple_(_Big_Temple).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Brihadisvara_Temple,_Thanjavur" title="Brihadisvara Temple, Thanjavur">Brihadisvara Temple, Thanjavur</a> constructed by <a href="/wiki/Rajendra_Chola_I" title="Rajendra Chola I">Rajendra Chola</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Until the 13th century, there was no less than 20 to 40 different states on the Indian Subcontinent which hosted a variety of cultures, languages, writing systems and religions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> At the beginning of the time period <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> was predominant throughout the area with the short-lived <a href="/wiki/Pala_Empire" title="Pala Empire">Pala Empire</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Gangetic_Plain" title="Indo-Gangetic Plain">Indo Gangetic Plain</a> sponsoring the faith's institutions. One such institution was the Buddhist <a href="/wiki/Nalanda_University" title="Nalanda University">Nalanda University</a> in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar, India</a> a centre of scholarship and brought a divided South Asia onto the global intellectual stage. Another accomplishment was the invention of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chaturanga" title="Chaturanga">Chaturanga</a></i> game which later was exported to Europe and became <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">Chess</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup>
In Southern India, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> Kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Chola_dynasty" title="Chola dynasty">Chola</a> gained prominence with an overseas empire that controlled parts of modern-day Sri Lanka, Malaysia, and <a href="/wiki/Chola_invasion_of_Srivijaya" title="Chola invasion of Srivijaya">Indonesia</a> as oversees territories and accelerated the spread of Hinduism into the historic culture of these places.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup> In this time period, neighboring areas such as <a href="/wiki/History_of_Afghanistan" title="History of Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Tibet" title="History of Tibet">Tibet</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Southeast_Asia" title="History of Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> were under <a href="/wiki/Greater_India" title="Greater India">South Asian influence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1206 onward a series of <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquests_in_the_Indian_subcontinent" title="Muslim conquests in the Indian subcontinent">Turkic Islamic invasions</a> from modern-day Afghanistan and Iran conquered massive portions of Northern India, founding the <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Sultanate" title="Delhi Sultanate">Delhi Sultanate</a> which remained supreme until the 16th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016107_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016107-152">[150]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Decline_of_Buddhism_in_the_Indian_subcontinent" title="Decline of Buddhism in the Indian subcontinent">Buddhism declined</a> in South Asia vanishing in many areas but Hinduism survived and reinforced itself in areas conquered by <a href="/wiki/Hindu%E2%80%93Islamic_relations" title="Hindu–Islamic relations">Muslims</a>. In the far South, the Kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Vijayanagara_Empire" title="Vijayanagara Empire">Vijanyagar</a> was not conquered by any Muslim state in the period. The turn of the 16th century would see the rise of a new Islamic Empire – the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughals</a> and the establishment of European trade posts by the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India" title="Portuguese India">Portuguese</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast_Asia">Southeast Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Southeast Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Southeast_Asia#Medieval_History" title="History of Southeast Asia">History of Southeast Asia § Medieval History</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Borobdur9205.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="770" data-file-width="1216" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Borobdur9205.jpg/220px-Borobdur9205.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Borobdur9205.jpg/330px-Borobdur9205.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Borobdur9205.jpg/440px-Borobdur9205.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Borobdur9205.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of <a href="/wiki/Borobudur" title="Borobudur">Borobudur</a>, from center point of view. Located in <a href="/wiki/Magelang" title="Magelang">Megelang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Java" title="Central Java">Central Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>. Built in the 9th century Borobudur is the largest Buddhist Temple in the world.</div></div></div><p>From the 8th century onward Southeast Asia stood to benefit from the trade taking place between South and East Asia, numerous kingdoms arose in the region due to the flow of wealth passing through the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Malacca" title="Strait of Malacca">Strait of Malacca</a>. While Southeast Asia had numerous outside influences <a href="/wiki/Greater_India" title="Greater India">India</a> was the greatest source of inspiration for the region. North Vietnam as an exception was culturally closer to China for centuries due to conquest.
</p><p>Since rule from the third century BCE North Vietnam continued to be subjugated by Chinese states, although they continually resisted periodically. There were three periods of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_domination_of_Vietnam" title="Chinese domination of Vietnam">Chinese Domination</a> that spanned near 1100 years. The Vietnamese gained long lasting independence in the 10th century when China was <a href="/wiki/Five_Dynasties_and_Ten_Kingdoms_period" title="Five Dynasties and Ten Kingdoms period">divided</a> with <a href="/wiki/T%C4%A9nh_H%E1%BA%A3i_qu%C3%A2n" title="Tĩnh Hải quân">Tĩnh Hải quân</a> and the successor <a href="/wiki/%C4%90%E1%BA%A1i_Vi%E1%BB%87t" title="Đại Việt">Đại Việt</a>. Nonetheless, even as an independent state a sort of begrudging <a href="/wiki/Sinicization" title="Sinicization">sinicization</a> occurred. South Vietnam was governed by the ancient Hindu <a href="/wiki/Champa" title="Champa">Champa Kingdom</a> but was annexed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cham%E2%80%93Annamese_War" title="Cham–Annamese War">Vietnamese</a> in the 15th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup>
</p><p>The spread of <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> and maritime trade between China and <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a> created the foundation for Southeast Asia's first major empires; including the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Empire" title="Khmer Empire">Khmer Empire</a> from Cambodia and <a href="/wiki/Srivijaya" title="Srivijaya">Sri Vijaya</a> from Indonesia. During the Khmer Empire's height in the 12th century the city of <a href="/wiki/Angkor_Thom" title="Angkor Thom">Angkor Thom</a> was among the largest of the pre-modern world due to its water management. <a href="/wiki/Jayavarman_II" title="Jayavarman II">King Jayavarman II</a> constructed over a hundred hospitals throughout his realm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> Nearby rose the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pagan_Empire" title="Pagan Empire">Pagan Empire</a> in modern-day Burma, using elephants as military might.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-156">[154]</a></sup> The construction of the Buddhist <a href="/wiki/Shwezigon_Pagoda" title="Shwezigon Pagoda">Shwezigon Pagoda</a> and its tolerance for believers of older polytheistic gods helped <a href="/wiki/Theravada" title="Theravada">Theravada Buddhism</a> become supreme in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_156-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-156">[154]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Indonesia, <a href="/wiki/Srivijaya" title="Srivijaya">Srivijaya</a> from the 7th through 14th century was a <a href="/wiki/Thalassocracy" title="Thalassocracy">Thalassocracy</a> that focused on maritime city states and trade. Controlling the vital choke points of the <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Strait" title="Sunda Strait">Sunda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Malacca" title="Strait of Malacca">Malacca straits</a> it became rich from trade ranging from Japan through Arabia. Gold, Ivory and Ceramics were all major commodities traveling through port cities. The Empire was also responsible for the construction of wonders such as <a href="/wiki/Borobudur" title="Borobudur">Borobudur</a>. During this time Indonesian sailors crossed the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>; evidence suggests that they may have colonized <a href="/wiki/History_of_Madagascar" title="History of Madagascar">Madagascar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Madagascar_Founded_By_Women_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-Madagascar_Founded_By_Women-157">[155]</a></sup> Indian culture spread to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Philippines_(900%E2%80%931521)" title="History of the Philippines (900–1521)">Philippines</a>, likely through Indonesian trade resulting in the first documented use of writing in the archipelago and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indianized_kingdom" title="Indianized kingdom">Indianized kingdoms</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup>
</p><p>Over time changing economic and political conditions elsewhere and wars weakened the traditional empires of South East Asia.
While the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_and_conquests" title="Mongol invasions and conquests">Mongol Invasions</a> did not directly annex Southeast Asia the war-time devastation paved way for the rise of new nations. In the 14th century the Khmer Empire was uprooted by peristent years of war losing the functinality and engineerirng knowldege of its advanced water managment system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Srivijaya" title="Srivijaya">Sri Vijaya</a> was overtaken by the <a href="/wiki/Majapahit" title="Majapahit">Majapahit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup> Islamic missionaries and merchants arrived eventually leading to Islamization in Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[C]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Asia">East Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: East Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medieval_Asia" title="Medieval Asia">Medieval Asia</a></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palastexamen-SongDynastie.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="865" data-file-width="1262" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Palastexamen-SongDynastie.jpg/220px-Palastexamen-SongDynastie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Palastexamen-SongDynastie.jpg/330px-Palastexamen-SongDynastie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Palastexamen-SongDynastie.jpg/440px-Palastexamen-SongDynastie.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palastexamen-SongDynastie.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In China public examinations gave citizens the opportunity to be employed by the Imperial Government through <a href="/wiki/Meritocracy" title="Meritocracy">meritocracy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[161]</a></sup> The examination system reached its maximum effectiveness in the 11th–12th centuries. Painting from <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> era.</div></div></div><p> The time frame of 500–1500 in East Asia's history and China in particular has been proposed as an accurate classification for the region's history within the context of global Post-classical history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[162]</a></sup> There has been an attempt made within college courses to adapt the Post-Classical concept to eras in Chinese history. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[163]</a></sup>  Discussions within Columbia University’s Association of Asian studies have postulated that similarities between China and other regions of Eurasia during Post-Classical Times have often been overlooked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[D]</a></sup> Typically the English language histography of Japan postulates that its 'medieval period' began as late as 1185.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[E]</a></sup>
</p><p>During this period the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_world" title="Eastern world">Eastern world</a> empires continued to expand through trade, migration and conquests of neighboring areas. <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a> went under the process of voluntary <a href="/wiki/Sinicization" title="Sinicization">sinicization</a>, or the impression of Chinese cultural and political ideas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[170]</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Three_Kingdoms_of_Korea" title="Three Kingdoms of Korea">Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asuka_period" title="Asuka period">Japan</a> sinicized because their ruling class were largely impressed by China's bureaucracy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003126_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003126-176">[171]</a></sup> The major influences China had on these countries were the spread of Confucianism, the spread of Buddhism, and the establishment of centralized governance. Throughout East Asia, Buddhism was most visible in monasteries and local educational institutions and Confucianism remained the ideology of social cohesion and state power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003181_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003181-178">[173]</a></sup> In the times of the <a href="/wiki/Sui_dynasty" title="Sui dynasty">Sui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasties</a> (581–1279), China remained the world's largest economy and most technologically advanced society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[174]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[175]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Four_Great_Inventions" title="Four Great Inventions">Inventions</a> such as gunpowder, woodblock printing and the magnetic compass were improved upon. China stood in contrast to other areas at the time as the imperial governments exhibited concentrated central authority instead of <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudalism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[176]</a></sup>
</p><p>China exhibited much interest in <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_imperial_China" title="Foreign relations of imperial China">foreign affairs</a> during the Tang and Song dynasties. From the 7th through the 10th Tang China was focused on securing the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> as the selling of its goods westwards was central to the nation's economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003126_176-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003126-176">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[177]</a></sup> For a time China, successfully secured its frontiers by integrating their nomadic neighbors- the <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6kt%C3%BCrks" title="Göktürks">Gokturks</a> into their civilization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016149_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016149-183">[178]</a></sup> The Tang dynasty expanded into Central Asia and received tribute from Eastern Iran.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003126_176-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003126-176">[171]</a></sup> Western expansion ended with <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Talas" title="Battle of Talas">wars</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasid Caliphate</a> and the deadly <a href="/wiki/An_Lushan_Rebellion" title="An Lushan Rebellion">An Lushan Rebellion</a> which resulted in an deadly but uncertain death toll of millions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016156_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016156-184">[179]</a></sup>
</p><p>After the collapse of the Tang dynasty and subsequent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ten_Kingdoms_period" title="Ten Kingdoms period">civil wars</a> came the second phase of Chinese interest in foreign relations. Unlike the Tang, the Song specialized in overseas trade and peacefully created a maritime network and China's population became concentrated in the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003126–127_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003126–127-185">[180]</a></sup> Chinese merchant ships reached Indonesia, India and Arabia. Southeast Asia's economy flourished from trade with Song China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003132_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003132-186">[181]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%EB%AF%B8%EB%A5%B5%EB%B0%98%EA%B0%80%EC%82%AC%EC%9C%A0%EC%83%81_(%E5%BD%8C%E5%8B%92%E8%8F%A9%E8%96%A9%E5%8D%8A%E8%B7%8F%E6%80%9D%E6%83%9F%E5%83%8F).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="545" data-file-width="740" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/%EB%AF%B8%EB%A5%B5%EB%B0%98%EA%B0%80%EC%82%AC%EC%9C%A0%EC%83%81_%28%E5%BD%8C%E5%8B%92%E8%8F%A9%E8%96%A9%E5%8D%8A%E8%B7%8F%E6%80%9D%E6%83%9F%E5%83%8F%29.jpg/220px-%EB%AF%B8%EB%A5%B5%EB%B0%98%EA%B0%80%EC%82%AC%EC%9C%A0%EC%83%81_%28%E5%BD%8C%E5%8B%92%E8%8F%A9%E8%96%A9%E5%8D%8A%E8%B7%8F%E6%80%9D%E6%83%9F%E5%83%8F%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/%EB%AF%B8%EB%A5%B5%EB%B0%98%EA%B0%80%EC%82%AC%EC%9C%A0%EC%83%81_%28%E5%BD%8C%E5%8B%92%E8%8F%A9%E8%96%A9%E5%8D%8A%E8%B7%8F%E6%80%9D%E6%83%9F%E5%83%8F%29.jpg/330px-%EB%AF%B8%EB%A5%B5%EB%B0%98%EA%B0%80%EC%82%AC%EC%9C%A0%EC%83%81_%28%E5%BD%8C%E5%8B%92%E8%8F%A9%E8%96%A9%E5%8D%8A%E8%B7%8F%E6%80%9D%E6%83%9F%E5%83%8F%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/%EB%AF%B8%EB%A5%B5%EB%B0%98%EA%B0%80%EC%82%AC%EC%9C%A0%EC%83%81_%28%E5%BD%8C%E5%8B%92%E8%8F%A9%E8%96%A9%E5%8D%8A%E8%B7%8F%E6%80%9D%E6%83%9F%E5%83%8F%29.jpg/440px-%EB%AF%B8%EB%A5%B5%EB%B0%98%EA%B0%80%EC%82%AC%EC%9C%A0%EC%83%81_%28%E5%BD%8C%E5%8B%92%E8%8F%A9%E8%96%A9%E5%8D%8A%E8%B7%8F%E6%80%9D%E6%83%9F%E5%83%8F%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%EB%AF%B8%EB%A5%B5%EB%B0%98%EA%B0%80%EC%82%AC%EC%9C%A0%EC%83%81_(%E5%BD%8C%E5%8B%92%E8%8F%A9%E8%96%A9%E5%8D%8A%E8%B7%8F%E6%80%9D%E6%83%9F%E5%83%8F).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Japanese Buddha sculpture from the <a href="/wiki/Asuka_period" title="Asuka period">Asuka Period</a></div></div></div>
<p>With the country's emphasis on trade and economic growth, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Song_dynasty" title="Economy of the Song dynasty">Song China's economy</a> began to use machines to manufacture goods and coal as a source of energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016160_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016160-187">[182]</a></sup> The advances of the Song in the 11th/12th centuries have been considered an early <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_industrialization" title="Chinese industrialization">industrial revolution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[183]</a></sup> Economic advancements came at the cost of military affairs and the Song became open to invasions from the north. China became divided as Song's northern lands were conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Jurchen_people" title="Jurchen people">Jurchen people</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[184]</a></sup> By 1200 there were five Chinese kingdoms stretching from modern day Turkestan to the Sea of Japan including the <a href="/wiki/Qara_Khitai" title="Qara Khitai">Western Liao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Xia" title="Western Xia">Western Xia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115–1234)">Jin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Southern Song</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dali_Kingdom" title="Dali Kingdom">Dali</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[185]</a></sup> Because these states competed with each other they all were eventually annexed by the rising <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a> before 1279.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[186]</a></sup>
</p><p>After seventy years of <a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_China" title="Mongol conquest of China">conquest</a>, the Mongols proclaimed the <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan dynasty</a> and also annexed <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Korea" title="Mongol invasions of Korea">Korea</a>; they failed to conquer <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Japan" title="Mongol invasions of Japan">Japan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003128–129_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003128–129-192">[187]</a></sup> Mongol conquerors also made China accessible to <a href="/wiki/Europeans_in_Medieval_China" title="Europeans in Medieval China">European travelers</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[188]</a></sup> The Mongol era was short lived due to plagues and famine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[189]</a></sup> After <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Turban_Rebellion" title="Red Turban Rebellion">revolution</a> in 1368 the succeeding <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> ushered in a period of prosperity and brief <a href="/wiki/Ming_treasure_voyages" title="Ming treasure voyages">foreign expeditions</a> before isolating itself from global affairs for centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[190]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Joseon" title="Joseon">Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muromachi_period" title="Muromachi period">Japan</a> however continued to have relations with China and with other Asian countries. In the 15th century <a href="/wiki/Sejong_the_Great" title="Sejong the Great">Sejong the Great</a>  of Korea cemented his country's identity by creating the <a href="/wiki/Hangul" title="Hangul">Hangul Writing</a> system to replace use of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_characters" title="Chinese characters">Chinese Characters</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[191]</a></sup> Meanwhile, Japan fell under military rule of the <a href="/wiki/Kamakura_period" title="Kamakura period">Kamakura</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Ashikaga_shogunate" title="Ashikaga shogunate">Ashikaga</a> Shogunate dominated by <a href="/wiki/Samurai" title="Samurai">Samurai</a> warriors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[192]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Americas">The Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: The Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">Pre-Columbian era</a></div>
<p>The Postclassical Era of the Americas can be considered set at a different time span from that of Afro-Eurasia. As the developments of Mesoamerican and Andean civilization differ greatly from that of the Old World, as well as the speed at which it developed, the Postclassical Era in the traditional sense does not take place until near the end of the medieval age in Western Europe. As such, for the purposes of this article, the <a href="/wiki/Woodland_period" title="Woodland period">Woodland period</a> and <a href="/wiki/Classic_stage" title="Classic stage">Classic stage</a> of the Americas will be discussed here, which takes place from about 400 to 1400.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[193]</a></sup> For the technical Postclassical stage in American development which took place on the eve of European contact, see <a href="/wiki/Post-Classic_stage" title="Post-Classic stage">Post-Classic stage</a>.
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1021810730" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="mod-gallery mod-gallery-default mod-gallery-center"><div class="title"><div>Maps depicting the Western Hemisphere</div></div><div class="main"><div><ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional nochecker bordered-images whitebg">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 385px"><div style="width: 385px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 380px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:North_American_cultural_areas.png" title="Cultural areas of North America prior to European Contact"><img alt="Cultural areas of North America prior to European Contact" data-file-height="1700" data-file-width="1490" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/North_American_cultural_areas.png/175px-North_American_cultural_areas.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/North_American_cultural_areas.png/263px-North_American_cultural_areas.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/North_American_cultural_areas.png/351px-North_American_cultural_areas.png 2x" width="175"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Cultural areas of North America prior to European Contact
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 385px"><div style="width: 385px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 380px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%C3%81reas_Culturales_de_Am%C3%A9rica.PNG" title="Cultural areas of South and Central America prior to European contact, (in Spanish)."><img alt="Cultural areas of South and Central America prior to European contact, (in Spanish)." data-file-height="624" data-file-width="596" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/%C3%81reas_Culturales_de_Am%C3%A9rica.PNG/191px-%C3%81reas_Culturales_de_Am%C3%A9rica.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/%C3%81reas_Culturales_de_Am%C3%A9rica.PNG/287px-%C3%81reas_Culturales_de_Am%C3%A9rica.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/%C3%81reas_Culturales_de_Am%C3%A9rica.PNG/382px-%C3%81reas_Culturales_de_Am%C3%A9rica.PNG 2x" width="191"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Cultural areas of South and Central America prior to European contact, (in Spanish).
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
</ul></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As a continent there was little unified trade or communication. Advances in agriculture spread northward from <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</a> indirectly through trade. Major cultural areas however still developed independently of each other.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Norse_Contact_and_the_Polar_Regions">Norse Contact and the Polar Regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Norse Contact and the Polar Regions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Norse_colonization_of_North_America" title="Norse colonization of North America">Norse colonization of North America</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Authentic_Viking_recreation.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Authentic_Viking_recreation.jpg/220px-Authentic_Viking_recreation.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Authentic_Viking_recreation.jpg/330px-Authentic_Viking_recreation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Authentic_Viking_recreation.jpg/440px-Authentic_Viking_recreation.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Authentic_Viking_recreation.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Authentic reconstruction of Norse site at <a href="/wiki/L%27Anse_aux_Meadows" title="L'Anse aux Meadows">L'Anse aux Meadows</a>. Photo provided by Dylan Kereluk.</div></div></div>
<p>While there was little regular contact between the Americas and the Old World the <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Norse Vikings</a> explored and even colonized <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> as early as 1000. None of these settlements survived past <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Medieval Times</a>. Outside of Scandinavia knowledge of the discovery of the Americas was interpreted as a <a href="/wiki/Vinland#Medieval_geographers" title="Vinland">remote island</a> or the <a href="/wiki/North_Pole" title="North Pole">North Pole</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[194]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><audio class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="504" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Saga_of_Eirik_the_Red._Chapter_8-11.ogg" id="mwe_player_5" preload="none" style="width:220px;" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="44303" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (44 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c7/Saga_of_Eirik_the_Red._Chapter_8-11.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/></audio> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saga_of_Eirik_the_Red._Chapter_8-11.ogg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Recording of Saga of Eirik the Red. Chapter 8-11 describing interactions between the Norse and <a href="/wiki/Beothuk" title="Beothuk">Beothuk</a> erroniously called <a href="/wiki/Eskimo" title="Eskimo">Eskimo</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The Norse arriving from Greenland settled Greenland from approximately 980 to 1450.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-200">[195]</a></sup> The Norse arrived in southern <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> prior to the 13th century approach of <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> <a href="/wiki/Thule_people" title="Thule people">Thule people</a> in the area. The extent of the interaction between the Norse and Thule is unclear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_200-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-200">[195]</a></sup> Greenland was valuable to the Norse due to trade of ivory that came from the tusks of walruses. The <a href="/wiki/Little_Ice_Age" title="Little Ice Age">Little Ice Age</a> adversely affected the colonies and they vanished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_200-2"><a href="#cite_note-:2-200">[195]</a></sup> Greenland would be lost to Europeans until <a href="/wiki/Danish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Danish colonization of the Americas">Danish Colonization</a> in the 18th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[196]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Norse also explored and colonized farther south in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newfoundland" title="Newfoundland">Newfoundland Canada</a> at <a href="/wiki/L%27Anse_aux_Meadows" title="L'Anse aux Meadows">L'Anse aux Meadows</a> referred to by the Norse as <i><a href="/wiki/Vinland" title="Vinland">Vinland</a></i>. The colony at most existed for twenty years and resulted in no known transmission of diseases or technology to the <a href="/wiki/First_Nations_in_Canada" title="First Nations in Canada">First Nations</a>. To the Norse <i>Vinland</i> was known for plentiful grape vines to make superior wine. One reason for the colony's failure was constant violence with the native <a href="/wiki/Beothuk" title="Beothuk">Beothuk</a> tribe who the Norse referred to as <a href="/wiki/Skr%C3%A6ling" title="Skræling">Skraeling</a>.
</p><p>After initial expeditions there is a possibility that the Norse continued to visit modern day Canada. Surviving records from medieval Iceland indicate some sporadic voyages to a land called <i><a href="/wiki/Markland" title="Markland">Markland</a></i>, possibly the coast of <a href="/wiki/Labrador" title="Labrador">Labrador, Canada</a>, as late as 1347 presumably to collect wood for deforested Greenland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[197]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Areas">Northern Areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Northern Areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
