<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Canada#Post-Archaic_periods" title="Indigenous peoples in Canada">Indigenous peoples in Canada § Post-Archaic periods</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Native_Americans_in_the_United_States#Major_cultures" title="History of Native Americans in the United States">History of Native Americans in the United States § Major cultures</a></div><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mississippi_Pipe_bowl_chunkey_player_EthnM.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2621" data-file-width="1971" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Mississippi_Pipe_bowl_chunkey_player_EthnM.jpg/100px-Mississippi_Pipe_bowl_chunkey_player_EthnM.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Mississippi_Pipe_bowl_chunkey_player_EthnM.jpg/150px-Mississippi_Pipe_bowl_chunkey_player_EthnM.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Mississippi_Pipe_bowl_chunkey_player_EthnM.jpg/200px-Mississippi_Pipe_bowl_chunkey_player_EthnM.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mississippi_Pipe_bowl_chunkey_player_EthnM.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mississippi Pipe bowl chunkey player EthnM</div></div></div><p>In northern <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, many <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherer</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agricultural" title="Agricultural">agricultural</a> societies thrived in the diverse region. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_in_the_United_States" title="Native American in the United States">Native American tribes</a> varied greatly in characteristics; some, including the <a href="/wiki/Mound_Builders" title="Mound Builders">Mound Builders</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Oasisamerica" title="Oasisamerica">Oasisamerican cultures</a> were complex chiefdoms. Other nations which inhabited the states of the modern northern United States and Canada had less complexity and did not follow technological changes as quickly. Approximately around the year 500 during the <a href="/wiki/Woodland_period" title="Woodland period">Woodland period</a>, Native Americans began to transition to bows and arrows from spears for hunting and warfare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[198]</a></sup> Technological advancement however was uneven. During the 12th century was the widespread adoption of Corn as a staple crop in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_United_States" title="Eastern United States">Eastern United States</a>. Corn would continue to be the staple crop of natives in the Eastern United States and Canada until the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbian_Exchange" title="Columbian Exchange">Colombian Exchange</a>.
</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stonework_Mesa_Verde_National_Park_Colorado_USA.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Stonework_Mesa_Verde_National_Park_Colorado_USA.JPG/100px-Stonework_Mesa_Verde_National_Park_Colorado_USA.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Stonework_Mesa_Verde_National_Park_Colorado_USA.JPG/150px-Stonework_Mesa_Verde_National_Park_Colorado_USA.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Stonework_Mesa_Verde_National_Park_Colorado_USA.JPG/199px-Stonework_Mesa_Verde_National_Park_Colorado_USA.JPG 2x" width="100"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stonework_Mesa_Verde_National_Park_Colorado_USA.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stonework Mesa Verde National Park Colorado</div></div></div>
<p>In the eastern United States, rivers were the medium of trade and communication. <a href="/wiki/Cahokia" title="Cahokia">Cahokia</a> located in the modern U.S <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Illinois" title="State of Illinois">State of Illinois</a> was among the most significant city within the <a href="/wiki/Mississippian_culture" title="Mississippian culture">Mississippian culture</a>. Focused around <a href="/wiki/Monks_Mound" title="Monks Mound">Monks Mound</a> archaeology indicates the population increased exponentially after 1000 because it manufactured important tools for agriculture and hosted cultural attractions. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016393_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016393-204">[199]</a></sup> Around 1350 Cahokia was abandoned, environmental factors have been proposed for the city's decline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[200]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the same time Ancestral Puebloans constructed clusters of buildings in the <a href="/wiki/Chaco_Culture_National_Historical_Park" title="Chaco Culture National Historical Park">Chaco Canyon</a> site located in the <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">State of New Mexico</a>. Individual houses may have been occupied by more than 600 residents at any one time. Chaco Canyon was the only pre-Columbian site in the United States to build paved roads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[201]</a></sup> Pottery indicates a society that was becoming more complex, turkeys for the first time in the continental United States were also domesticated. Around 1150 the structures of Chaco Canyon were abandoned, likely as a result of severe drought.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[202]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016391_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016391-208">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[204]</a></sup> There were also other Pueblo complexes in the Southwestern United States. After reaching climaxes native complex societies in the United States declined and did not entirely recover before the arrival of European Explorers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[205]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[F]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Mesoamerica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Telamones_Tula.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Telamones_Tula.jpg/220px-Telamones_Tula.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Telamones_Tula.jpg/330px-Telamones_Tula.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Telamones_Tula.jpg/440px-Telamones_Tula.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Telamones_Tula.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Toltec <a href="/wiki/Atlantean_figures" title="Atlantean figures">Atlantean figures</a> at the Tula site. The <a href="/wiki/Toltec" title="Toltec">Toltec Civilization</a> inspired the later <a href="/wiki/Aztecs" title="Aztecs">Aztecs</a>.</div></div></div><p>At the beginning of the global Post Classic Period, the city of <a href="/wiki/Teotihuacan" title="Teotihuacan">Teotihuacan</a> was at its zenith, housing over 125,000 people, at 500 A.D it was the sixth largest city in the world at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[207]</a></sup> The city's residents built the <a href="/wiki/Pyramid_of_the_Sun" title="Pyramid of the Sun">Pyramid of the Sun</a> the third largest pyramid of the world, oriented to follow astronomical events. Suddenly in the 6th and 7th centuries, the city suddenly declined possibly as a result of severe environmental damage caused by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extreme_weather_events_of_535%E2%80%93536" title="Extreme weather events of 535–536">extreme weather events of 535–536</a>. There is evidence that large parts of the city were burned, possibly in a domestic rebellion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[G]</a></sup> The city's legacy would inspire all future civilizations in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[211]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the same time was Classic Age of the <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Mayan Civilization</a> clustered in dozens of city states on the <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula" title="Yucatán Peninsula">Yucatán</a> and modern day <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[212]</a></sup> The most significant of these cities was <a href="/wiki/Chichen_Itza" title="Chichen Itza">Chichen Itza</a> which often fiercely competed with its neighbors to be the dominant economic influence in the region.
</p><p>
The Mayans had an upper caste of priests, who were well versed in astronomy, mathematics and writing. The Mayan developed the concept of zero, and a 365-day calendar which possibly pre-dates its creation in Old-World societies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[213]</a></sup> After 900, many Mayan cities suddenly declined in a period of drought.</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:186px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aztec11_Bloodletting.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="560" decoding="async" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Aztec11_Bloodletting.jpg/184px-Aztec11_Bloodletting.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Aztec11_Bloodletting.jpg/276px-Aztec11_Bloodletting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Aztec11_Bloodletting.jpg/368px-Aztec11_Bloodletting.jpg 2x" width="184"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aztec11_Bloodletting.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aztec Bloodletting, priests conduct a heart sacrifice, from the <i>Tudela Codex</i>, 16th century.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Toltec_Empire" title="Toltec Empire">Toltec Empire</a> arose from the <a href="/wiki/Toltec" title="Toltec">Toltec</a> culture, and were remembered as wise and benevolent leaders. One priest-king called <a href="/wiki/Ce_Acatl_Topiltzin" title="Ce Acatl Topiltzin">Ce Acatl Topiltzin</a> advocated against human sacrifice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-:8-221">[214]</a></sup> After his death in 947, civil wars of religious character broke out between those who supported and opposed Topiltzin's teachings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_221-1"><a href="#cite_note-:8-221">[214]</a></sup> Modern historians however are skeptical of the extent of Toltec and influence and believe that much of the information known about the Toltecs was created by the later Aztecs as an inspiration myth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[215]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 1300s, a small band of violent, religious radicals called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">Aztecs</a> began minor raids throughout the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003148_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003148-223">[216]</a></sup> Eventually they began to claim connections with the Toltec civilization, and insisted they were the rightful successors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[217]</a></sup> They began to grow in numbers and conquer large areas of land. Fundamental to their conquest, was the use of <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">political terror</a> in the sense that the Aztec leaders and priests would command the <a href="/wiki/Human_sacrifice" title="Human sacrifice">human sacrifice</a> of their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conquest_(military)#Subjugation" title="Conquest (military)">subjugated</a> people as means of humility and coercion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003148_223-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003148-223">[216]</a></sup> Most of the Mesoamerican region would eventually fall under the Aztec Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003148_223-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003148-223">[216]</a></sup> On the <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula" title="Yucatán Peninsula">Yucatán Peninsula</a> most of the <a href="/wiki/Maya_peoples" title="Maya peoples">Mayan People</a> continued to be independent of the Aztecs but their traditional civilization declined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003149_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003149-225">[218]</a></sup> Aztec developments expanded cultivation, applying the use of <a href="/wiki/Chinampa" title="Chinampa">chinampas</a>, irrigation, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terrace_agriculture" title="Terrace agriculture">terrace agriculture</a>; important crops included <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potatoes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Avocado" title="Avocado">avocados</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003148_223-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003148-223">[216]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1430 the city of <a href="/wiki/Tenochtitlan" title="Tenochtitlan">Tenochtitlan</a> allied with other powerful <a href="/wiki/Nahuan_languages" title="Nahuan languages">Nahuatl</a> speaking cities- <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texcoco_(altepetl)" title="Texcoco (altepetl)">Texcoco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tlacopan" title="Tlacopan">Tlacopan</a> to create the Aztec Empire otherwise known as Triple-Alliance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003149_225-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003149-225">[218]</a></sup> Though referred to as an empire the Aztec Empire functioned as a system of tribute collection with Tenochtitlan at its center. By the turn of the 16th century "<a href="/wiki/Flower_war" title="Flower war">flower wars</a>" between the Aztecs and rival states such as <a href="/wiki/Tlaxcala_(Nahua_state)" title="Tlaxcala (Nahua state)">Tlaxcala</a> had continued for over fifty years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[219]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_America">South America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: South America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era#South_America" title="Pre-Columbian era">Pre-Columbian era § South America</a></div>
<p>South American civilization was concentrated in the Andean region which had already hosted complex cultures since 2,500 BC. East of the Andean region, societies were generally semi nomadic. Discoveries on the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_basin" title="Amazon basin">Amazon River Basin</a> indicate the region likely had a pre-contact population of five million people and hosted complex societies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[220]</a></sup> Around the continent numerous agricultural peoples from <a href="/wiki/History_of_Colombia" title="History of Colombia">Colombia</a> to <a href="/wiki/History_of_Argentina" title="History of Argentina">Argentina</a> steadily advanced through numerous stages of development from 500 AD until European contact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[221]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Andean_Region">Andean Region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Andean Region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Andean_civilizations" title="Andean civilizations">Andean civilizations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Temple_of_the_Sun,_Machu_Picchu,_Peru_-_panoramio_(1).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1740" data-file-width="1096" decoding="async" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Temple_of_the_Sun%2C_Machu_Picchu%2C_Peru_-_panoramio_%281%29.jpg/150px-Temple_of_the_Sun%2C_Machu_Picchu%2C_Peru_-_panoramio_%281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Temple_of_the_Sun%2C_Machu_Picchu%2C_Peru_-_panoramio_%281%29.jpg/225px-Temple_of_the_Sun%2C_Machu_Picchu%2C_Peru_-_panoramio_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Temple_of_the_Sun%2C_Machu_Picchu%2C_Peru_-_panoramio_%281%29.jpg/300px-Temple_of_the_Sun%2C_Machu_Picchu%2C_Peru_-_panoramio_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Temple_of_the_Sun,_Machu_Picchu,_Peru_-_panoramio_(1).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Temple of the Sun, Machu Picchu, Peru, provided by David Broad.</div></div></div>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/Ancient_history" title="Ancient history">Ancient times</a> the Andean Region had developed civilizations independent of outside influences including that of <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[222]</a></sup> Through the Post Classical era a cycle of civilizations continued until <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Inca_Empire" title="Spanish conquest of the Inca Empire">Spanish contact</a>. Collectively Andean societies lacked currency, a written language and solid draft animals enjoyed by old world civilizations. Instead Andeans developed other methods to foster their growth, including use of the <a href="/wiki/Quipu" title="Quipu">quipu</a> system to communicate messages, llamas to carry smaller loads and an economy based on <a href="/wiki/Reciprocity_(social_and_political_philosophy)" title="Reciprocity (social and political philosophy)">reciprocity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003148_223-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003148-223">[216]</a></sup> Societies were often based on strict social hierarchies and economic redistribution from the ruling class.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003148_223-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003148-223">[216]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the first half of the Post Classical Period the Andean Region was dominated by two almost equally powerful states. In the North of Peru was the <a href="/wiki/Wari_Empire" title="Wari Empire">Wari Empire</a> and in the South of Peru and Bolivia there was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiwanaku_empire" title="Tiwanaku empire">Tiwanaku empire</a> both of whom were inspired by the earlier <a href="/wiki/Moche_culture" title="Moche culture">Moche People</a>. While the extent of their relationship to each other is unknown, it is believed that they were in a Cold-War with one another, competing but avoiding direct conflict to avoid <a href="/wiki/Mutual_assured_destruction" title="Mutual assured destruction">mutual assured destruction</a>. Without war there was prosperity and around the year 700 Tiwanaku city hosted a population of 1.4. million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[223]</a></sup> After the 8th century both states declined due to changing environmental conditions, laying the ground work for the Incas to emerge as a distinct culture centuries later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016387_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016387-231">[224]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 15th century the <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">Inca Empire</a> rose to annex all other nations in the area. Led by their sun-god king, <a href="/wiki/Sapa_Inca" title="Sapa Inca">Sapa Inca</a>, they slowly conquered what is now <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, and built their society throughout the Andes cultural region. The Incas spoke the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechua_languages" title="Quechua languages">Quechua languages</a>. The Incas used the advances created by earlier Andean societies. Incas have been known to have used <a href="/wiki/Abacus" title="Abacus">abacuses</a> to calculate mathematics. The Inca Empire is known for some of its magnificent structures, such as <a href="/wiki/Machu_Picchu" title="Machu Picchu">Machu Picchu</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cusco_region" title="Cusco region">Cusco region</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016389_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson2016389-232">[225]</a></sup> The empire expanded quickly northwards to Ecuador, Southwards to central Chile. To the north of the Inca Empire remained the independent <a href="/wiki/Tairona" title="Tairona">Tairona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muisca_Confederation" title="Muisca Confederation">Muisca Confederation</a> who practiced agriculture and gold metallurgy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[226]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[227]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1021810730" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="mod-gallery mod-gallery-default mod-gallery-center"><div class="title"><div>Maps depicting Oceania</div></div><div class="main"><div><ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional nochecker bordered-images whitebg">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 385px"><div style="width: 385px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 380px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aboriginal_regions.png" title="Map of the Aboriginal regions in Australia"><img alt="Map of the Aboriginal regions in Australia." data-file-height="1278" data-file-width="1425" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Aboriginal_regions.png/223px-Aboriginal_regions.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Aboriginal_regions.png/335px-Aboriginal_regions.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Aboriginal_regions.png/446px-Aboriginal_regions.png 2x" width="223"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Map of the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australians" title="Indigenous Australians">Aboriginal</a> regions in Australia
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 385px"><div style="width: 385px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 380px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Polynesian_Migration.svg" title="Colonization of East Polynesia, and dispersal to more remote islands (including Hawaii, Easter Island, and New Zealand)"><img alt="Polynesian Colonization of East Polynesia, and dispersal to more remote islands (including Hawaii, Easter Island, and New Zealand)" data-file-height="553" data-file-width="553" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Polynesian_Migration.svg/200px-Polynesian_Migration.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Polynesian_Migration.svg/300px-Polynesian_Migration.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Polynesian_Migration.svg/400px-Polynesian_Migration.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Colonization of East Polynesia, and dispersal to more remote islands (including Hawaii, Easter Island, and New Zealand)
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
</ul></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Oceania" title="History of Oceania">History of Oceania</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Micronesian_navigational_chart.jpg"><img alt="Micronesian navigational chart" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1298" data-file-width="1860" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Micronesian_navigational_chart.jpg/220px-Micronesian_navigational_chart.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Micronesian_navigational_chart.jpg/330px-Micronesian_navigational_chart.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Micronesian_navigational_chart.jpg/440px-Micronesian_navigational_chart.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Micronesian_navigational_chart.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands_stick_chart" title="Marshall Islands stick chart">Micronesian navigational chart</a>, these were used by Polynesians to navigate through wind and water currents.</div></div></div>
<p>Separate from developments in <a href="/wiki/Afro-Eurasia" title="Afro-Eurasia">Afro-Eurasia</a> and the Americas the region of greater <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a> continued to develop independently of the outside world. In <a href="/wiki/History_of_Australia" title="History of Australia">Australia</a>, the society of <a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_Australians" title="Aboriginal Australians">Aborigines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesia</a> changed little through the Post Classical Period since their arrival in the area from Africa around 50,000 BC. The only outside contact were encounters with fishermen of <a href="/wiki/Makassan_contact_with_Australia" title="Makassan contact with Australia">Indonesian</a> origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[H]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[228]</a></sup>
</p><p>Polynesian and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Micronesian_peoples" title="Micronesian peoples">Micronesian peoples</a> are rooted from <a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_indigenous_peoples" title="Taiwanese indigenous peoples">Taiwan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> and began their migration into the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> from 3000 to 1500 BC.
<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-237">[229]</a></sup>
After the 4th century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Micronesian_people" title="Micronesian people">Micronesia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Polynesians" title="Polynesians">Polynesian</a> peoples began to explore the South Pacific and later constructed cities in previously uninhabitated areas including <a href="/wiki/Nan_Madol" title="Nan Madol">Nan Madol</a> <a href="/wiki/Mu%CA%BBa_(Tongatapu)" title="Muʻa (Tongatapu)">Mu'a</a> and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[I]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[231]</a></sup> Around 1200 AD the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tu%27i_Tonga_Empire" title="Tu'i Tonga Empire">Tu'i Tonga Empire</a> spread its influence far and wide throughout the South Pacific Islands, being described by academics as a maritime chiefdom which used trade networks to keep power centralized around the king's capital. Polynesians on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outrigger_canoe" title="Outrigger canoe">outrigger</a> canoes <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_navigation" title="Polynesian navigation">discovered</a> and colonized some of the last uninhabited islands of earth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_237-1"><a href="#cite_note-:5-237">[229]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Discovery_and_settlement_of_Hawaii" title="Discovery and settlement of Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_Zealand" title="History of New Zealand">New Zealand</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Easter_Island" title="History of Easter Island">Easter Island</a> were among the final places to be reached, settlers discovering pristine lands. <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_narrative" title="Polynesian narrative">Oral Tradition</a> claimed that navigator <a href="/wiki/Ui-te-Rangiora" title="Ui-te-Rangiora">Ui-te-Rangiora</a> discovered icebergs in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ocean" title="Southern Ocean">Southern Ocean</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[232]</a></sup> In exploring and settling, Polynesian settlers did not strike at random but used their knowledge of wind and water currents to reach their destinations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson20169_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergerIsraelMillerParkinson20169-242">[233]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Book-Hawaii-Vtorov-246.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Book-Hawaii-Vtorov-246.jpg/220px-Book-Hawaii-Vtorov-246.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Book-Hawaii-Vtorov-246.jpg/330px-Book-Hawaii-Vtorov-246.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Book-Hawaii-Vtorov-246.jpg/440px-Book-Hawaii-Vtorov-246.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Book-Hawaii-Vtorov-246.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hale_o_Keawe" title="Hale o Keawe">Hale o Keawe</a>, a restored <a href="/wiki/Heiau" title="Heiau">Heiau</a> in the U.S <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">State of Hawaii</a>, used as sacred temple and sacrificial altar. The statues represent traditional gods.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:War_canoes_(5178916728).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2303" data-file-width="4265" decoding="async" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/War_canoes_%285178916728%29.jpg/220px-War_canoes_%285178916728%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/War_canoes_%285178916728%29.jpg/330px-War_canoes_%285178916728%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/War_canoes_%285178916728%29.jpg/440px-War_canoes_%285178916728%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:War_canoes_(5178916728).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Authentic <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_culture" title="Māori culture">Maori</a> <a href="/wiki/Waka_(canoe)" title="Waka (canoe)">Waka</a>, used for warfare and navigation in <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a></div></div></div>
<p>On the settled islands some Polynesian groups became distinct from one another. A significant example being the <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_people" title="Māori people">Maori</a> of New Zealand. Other island systems kept in contact with each other, such as <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_(island)" title="Hawaii (island)">Hawaii</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Society_Islands" title="Society Islands">Society Islands</a>. Ecologically, Polynesians had the challenge of sustaining themselves within limited environments. Some settlements caused mass extinctions of some native plant and animal species over time by hunting species such as the <a href="/wiki/Moa" title="Moa">Moa</a> and introducing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polynesian_Rat" title="Polynesian Rat">Polynesian Rat</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_237-2"><a href="#cite_note-:5-237">[229]</a></sup> Easter Island settlers engaged in complete ecological destruction of their habtiat and their population crashed afterwards possibly due to the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Moai" title="Moai">Easter Island Statues</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[234]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[235]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[236]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[237]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[J]</a></sup> Other colonizing groups adapted to accommodate to the ecology of specific islands such as the <a href="/wiki/Moriori" title="Moriori">Moriori</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Chatham_Islands" title="Chatham Islands">Chatham Islands</a>.
</p><p>Europeans on their voyages visited many Pacific Islands in the 16th and 17th century, but most areas of Oceania were not colonized until after the <a href="/wiki/First_voyage_of_James_Cook" title="First voyage of James Cook">voyages</a> of British explorer <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> in the 1780s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003236_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003236-249">[239]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_the_period">End of the period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: End of the period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">Early modern period</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Genoese_world_map_1457._LOC_97690053.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6763" data-file-width="10465" decoding="async" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Genoese_world_map_1457._LOC_97690053.jpg/300px-Genoese_world_map_1457._LOC_97690053.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Genoese_world_map_1457._LOC_97690053.jpg/450px-Genoese_world_map_1457._LOC_97690053.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Genoese_world_map_1457._LOC_97690053.jpg/600px-Genoese_world_map_1457._LOC_97690053.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Genoese_world_map_1457._LOC_97690053.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Genoese_map" title="Genoese map">Genoese world map</a>, 1457 it suggests the possibility of sea travel to India from Western Europe though this had not yet been done at the time.</div></div></div>
<p>As the postclassical era drew to a close in the 15th century, many of the empires established throughout the period were in decline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003138–139_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003138–139-250">[240]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> would soon be overshadowed in the Mediterranean by both Islamic and Christian rivals including <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Genoa</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turks" title="Ottoman Turks">Ottoman Turks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[241]</a></sup> The Byzantines faced repeated attacks from eastern and western powers during the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Crusade" title="Fourth Crusade">Fourth Crusade</a>, and declined further until the loss of <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turks" title="Ottoman Turks">Ottoman Turks</a> in 1453.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003138–139_250-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003138–139-250">[240]</a></sup>
</p><p>The largest change came in terms of trade and technology. The global significance of the fall of the Byzantines was the disruption of overland routes between Asia and Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[242]</a></sup> Traditional dominance of <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">Nomadism</a> in Eurasia declined and the <a href="/wiki/Pax_Mongolica" title="Pax Mongolica">Pax Mongolica</a> which had allowed for interactions between different civilizations was no longer available. <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a> were conquered by <a href="/wiki/Gunpowder_empires" title="Gunpowder empires">gunpowder empires</a> which successfully utilized advances in military technology but closed the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[K]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[244]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:THE_FALL_OF_CONSTANTINOPLE,_ITALY,_PROBABLY_VENICE,_LATE_15THEARLY_16TH_CENTURY._Private_coll..jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1353" data-file-width="1965" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/THE_FALL_OF_CONSTANTINOPLE%2C_ITALY%2C_PROBABLY_VENICE%2C_LATE_15THEARLY_16TH_CENTURY._Private_coll..jpg/200px-THE_FALL_OF_CONSTANTINOPLE%2C_ITALY%2C_PROBABLY_VENICE%2C_LATE_15THEARLY_16TH_CENTURY._Private_coll..jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/THE_FALL_OF_CONSTANTINOPLE%2C_ITALY%2C_PROBABLY_VENICE%2C_LATE_15THEARLY_16TH_CENTURY._Private_coll..jpg/300px-THE_FALL_OF_CONSTANTINOPLE%2C_ITALY%2C_PROBABLY_VENICE%2C_LATE_15THEARLY_16TH_CENTURY._Private_coll..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/THE_FALL_OF_CONSTANTINOPLE%2C_ITALY%2C_PROBABLY_VENICE%2C_LATE_15THEARLY_16TH_CENTURY._Private_coll..jpg/400px-THE_FALL_OF_CONSTANTINOPLE%2C_ITALY%2C_PROBABLY_VENICE%2C_LATE_15THEARLY_16TH_CENTURY._Private_coll..jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:THE_FALL_OF_CONSTANTINOPLE,_ITALY,_PROBABLY_VENICE,_LATE_15THEARLY_16TH_CENTURY._Private_coll..jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The fall of Constantinople brought the last remnants of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Classical Roman Empire</a> to an end.</div></div></div>
<p>Europeans – specifically the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Kingdom of Portugal</a> and various Italian explorers – intended to replace land travel with sea travel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:11_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-:11-256">[245]</a></sup> Originally European exploration merely looked for new routes to reach known destinations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:11_256-1"><a href="#cite_note-:11-256">[245]</a></sup> Portuguese Explorer <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco De Gama</a> traveled to India by sea in 1498 by circumnavigating Africa around the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:12_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-:12-257">[246]</a></sup> India and the coast of Africa were already known to Europeans but none had attempted a large trading mission prior to that time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:12_257-1"><a href="#cite_note-:12-257">[246]</a></sup> Due to navigation advances Portugal would create a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">global colonial empire</a> beginning with the <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Malacca_(1511)" title="Capture of Malacca (1511)">conquest of Malacca</a> in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> from 1511.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003158_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003158-258">[247]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other Explorers such as the Spanish sponsored Italian <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> intended to engage in trade by traveling on unfamiliar routes west from Europe. The subsequent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_discovery_of_the_Americas" title="European discovery of the Americas">European discovery of the Americas</a> in 1492 resulted in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbian_Exchange" title="Columbian Exchange">Colombian exchange</a> and the world's first pan-oceanic <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003155_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003155-259">[248]</a></sup> Spanish Explorer <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">Ferdinand Magellan</a> performed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magellan%27s_circumnavigation" title="Magellan's circumnavigation">first known circumnavigation</a> of Earth in 1521.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003-260">[249]</a></sup> The transfer of goods and diseases across <a href="/wiki/Ocean" title="Ocean">oceans</a> was unprecedented in creating a more connected world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003159_261-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003159-261">[250]</a></sup> From developments in navigation and trade <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_history" title="Modern history">modern history</a> began.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003155_259-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarraclough2003155-259">[248]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1093669538">.mw-parser-output .portalbox{padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portalborder{border:solid #aaa 1px}.mw-parser-output .portalbox.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portalbox.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:175px;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portalborder>ul{padding:0.1em;background:#f9f9f9}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style><div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint plainlist portalbox tright" role="navigation">
<ul>
<li><span><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/P_history.svg/31px-P_history.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/P_history.svg/47px-P_history.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/P_history.svg/62px-P_history.svg.png 2x" width="31"/></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:History" title="Portal:History">History portal</a></span></li>
<li><span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="3002" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/28px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/42px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/56px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg 2x" width="28"/></a></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:World" title="Portal:World">World portal</a></span></li></ul></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Age_of_Empires_II" title="Age of Empires II">Age of Empires II</a> – A <a href="/wiki/PC_game" title="PC game">personal computer game</a> using Post-classical history as its setting.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ancient_history" title="Ancient history">Ancient history</a> – covers all human history/prehistory preceding the Postclassical Era.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">Classical antiquity</a> – centered in the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Basin</a>, the interlocking civilizations of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Ancient Rome</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">Early modern period</a> – succeeding global time period.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_the_world" title="Economic history of the world">Economic history of the world</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/History_of_cartography" title="History of cartography">History of cartography</a> – Covers history of cartography and includes images of maps from Post-classical times.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/History_by_period" title="History by period">History by period</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_Antiquity" title="Late Antiquity">Late Antiquity</a> (aka: <a href="/wiki/Dark_Ages_(historiography)" title="Dark Ages (historiography)">Dark Ages</a>) – mainland Europe and the Mediterranean Basin, transition from Classical Antiquity to the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_throughout_history" title="List of largest cities throughout history">List of largest cities throughout history</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-classical_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-columns references-column-width reflist-upper-alpha" style="column-width: 60em;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Post-Classical is often used to describe global history that took place during the time of the European Middle Ages (whose scope is entirely Euro-centric). The use of Post-Classical as a term for the period is sometimes disputed but is still used in academic circles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>This usage of Post-Classical 'World History' should not be confused with the Post-Classic period of Mesoamerica.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-35">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">To expand further- Oceania, Afro Eurasia and the Americas were seperated by hard oceanic barriers that prevented global interactions between them until the late 15th century. The existence of these three 'worlds' does not imply that all parts of each world-region were connected to themselves. In Afro-Eurasia for instance, South and Central Africa were certainly disconnected from the greater contiental networks as were remote areas of Siberia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-163"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-163">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Islamization took place across different regions of Eurasia. However the Islamization that took place in maratime Southeast Asia contrast with that of  Central Asia. In South East Asia the approach of Islam was a bottom-up process where certain indivuals and groups began to convert due to percevied advantages. Meanwhile Central Asia's conversion was a top-down process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-169"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-169">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Within this model the greatest similarities that China had to Western Asia and Europe took place between 200-1000 CE. Similarities included both a breakdown in central authority (during the Three Kingdoms and Europe's Early Middle Ages) as well as the creation of large decentralized multi-ethnic empires (Tang Dynasty and Umayyad Caliphate).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[165]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-172"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-172">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This corresponds with the end of the Gempi War and the establishment of the 'Shogun' title. The imperial Yamato Dynasty and their civilian administration in Kyoto continued to exist but held little actual power. Japan would be under military control until 1868.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[167]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-212"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-212">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Typically in North American archaeology the post classical era starts at 1200, differing from the world-history usage of the term and the Measoamerican context as well<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[206]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-217"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-217">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This weather event was worldwide as has been demonstrated by dendroclimatology, it was also documented by Byzantine historians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[209]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[210]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-235"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-235">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Makassar people approached Australia on seasonal missions in search of Sea Cucumber, first arriving between 1500-1720, after the Post-Classical Period.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-239"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-239">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The growth of Polynesian settlement has been proposed as a possible start date for the entire era in world history <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[230]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-248"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-248">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The decline of Norse Greenland has been compared to that of Easter Island as both were isolated island societies that practiced deforestation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[238]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-254"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-254">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The use of 'closed' can be problematic because oftentimes Islamic regimes did not totally forbid Christian travel but would instead levy high tariffs. While some Europeans, including <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venice</a>, still took part in trade most Europeans were unwilling to pay tariffs in the long term<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[243]</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div>

<li id="cite_note-Haub1650-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Haub1650_9-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Haub (1995): "The average annual rate of growth was actually lower from 1 A.D. to 1650 than the rate suggested above for the 8000 B.C. to 1 A.D. period. One reason for this abnormally slow growth was the Black Plague. This dreaded scourge was not limited to 14th century Europe. The epidemic may have begun about 542 A.D. in Western Asia, spreading from there. It is believed that half the Byzantine Empire was destroyed in the 6th century, a total of 100 million deaths."</span>
